Sometimes we find someone who becomes our fate.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430083i/862106.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Caleb and Olivia was one of those stories. For years and years, with every obstacle possible thrown in their away they were never able to stay away from the other. <br>No matter how many times life screwed with them, they would always end up in each other’s path again. There are loves bigger than life itself. There are people who are meant to be. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430083i/862107.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was not a perfect love story. It was hard, consuming, painful, hurtful and sometimes simply wonderful. <br>But it was their story. Their love was amazingly beautiful in its own broken way and I feel lucky for having the chance to read their story.<br><br>This will definitely become a series that will remain with me for a long time. <br>Tarryn Fisher, without a doubt, was capable of turning a simple love story into a masterpiece.<br>I really advise you to read these series. ;) <br><br>(And now the important part: Look at that cover. However, since Ms. Fisher slipped me a literary roofie that made me feel compelled to read all three of these damn books she gets a bonus star.</s> You know, what? Screw it. 1 Star. This was a waste . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>I really didn’t enjoy <b>any</b> of these books except for <i>The Opportunist</i>. Rehashing the same story from a different character’s p</span>
  <span id="freeText7392678911604763018" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Good news is, I finished the series. <s>Bad news is, I could totally give this 1 Star and not feel bad about it. However, since Ms. Fisher slipped me a literary roofie that made me feel compelled to read all three of these damn books she gets a bonus star.</s> You know, what? Screw it. 1 Star. This was a waste . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448296961ra/17119548.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I really didn’t enjoy <b>any</b> of these books except for <i>The Opportunist</i>. Rehashing the same story from a different character’s point of view gets tiring, and reading the same story a <b>THIRD</b> time? Someone stick a fork in my eyeballs for me. <br><br>So, what did I learn upon finishing <i>Thief</i>? Well, I confirmed there ain’t nothing as angsty as New Adult. I feel the only fitting way to explain the <i>e – m – o – t – i – o – n</i> in this final story is via musical giffery. The only way to describe Caleb and Olivia’s on again/off again love is . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448296961ra/17119549.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I mean these two were seriously crazy in love . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448296962ra/17119550.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But <b>NOTHING</b> ever happened except stuff that pissed me off. I mean we’re not even talking about . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448296962ra/17119551.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>How’d that Bieber cover get in here? Erica must’ve hacked my ‘puter. Let me get that terrifying image out of your mind and replace it with the sexy original . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448297088ra/17119568.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Mmmmmm, that Usher. He sure has a good set of . . . . lungs on him, doesn’t he?<br><br>Now where was I? Oh yeah, the nothing happening. These two didn’t even bother making hang-up calls on each other. Instead, they drug their non-talking and miscommunicating on for <b>TEN MOTHERF-ING YEARS</b>, Caleb maybe fathered a baby (but made sure he did the right thing by completely abandoning it for years before a paternity test *eyeroll*), Olivia did the right thing by defending serial rapists and being “faithful” to her husband (*eyeroll*), I felt like I read 1,500 pages only to find out it was really less than 300, and in the end I was left with only one song I wanted to sing . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">

    <a title="It&#39;s just me Shelly B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3716081-it-s-just-me-shelly-b"><img alt="It&#39;s just me Shelly B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374929701p2/3716081.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="It&#39;s just me Shelly B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="It&#39;s just me Shelly B" href="/user/show/3716081-it-s-just-me-shelly-b">It&#39;s just me Shelly B</a>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer8603002362292149750">Thief (Love Me With Lies, #3) OMG this book was soooooo GOOD!!!!!!<br/> <br/>“Olivia. I’ve lost her three times. The first was to impatience. The second was to a lie so dense we couldn’t work our way through it, and the third time — this time — I’ve lost her to Noah”<br/> <br/>Caleb and Olivia met under a tree 10 years ago and they have been obsessed with each other ever since that day. This is the third and final book in this messy love affair and it was a GOOD one to end this series on! This isn't a pretty little</span>
  <span id="freeText8603002362292149750" style="display:none">Thief (Love Me With Lies, #3) OMG this book was soooooo GOOD!!!!!!<br /> <br />“Olivia. I’ve lost her three times. The first was to impatience. The second was to a lie so dense we couldn’t work our way through it, and the third time — this time — I’ve lost her to Noah”<br /> <br />Caleb and Olivia met under a tree 10 years ago and they have been obsessed with each other ever since that day. This is the third and final book in this messy love affair and it was a GOOD one to end this series on! This isn't a pretty little love story wrapped in a shiny little box with a bow....NO...it's messy all the way around!! But it's soooooo good!! I may repeat that few times!!<br /> <br />They have both lied, cheated, manipulated, they have loved others but it never fails they can't stay away from each other either......it's an obsession and one they will never get away from.<br /> <br />“I’ve rarely found a woman who I actually think is interesting. I like her darkness, her ever present sarcasm, the way she makes me work for every smile — every kiss. I like how strong she is, how hard she fights for things. I love how weak I make her. I might be her only weakness. I earned that spot and I very much want to keep it”<br /> <br />They come together and something always tears them apart.However Caleb is done he is ready to fight for the woman that he's been in love with for 10 years!!!! That's right Caleb....FIGHT for her!!!!!!<br /> <br />“My competition is good. Undoubtedly he’s never lied to her, broken her heart or married another woman to spite her. But she’s mine, and I’m not giving her up without a fight this time”<br /> <br />Will he get his girl or will fate just keep pulling them away?They both love each other deeply but so much has happened between them......will they ever make it?<br /> <br />Let's hope love is enough...but to quote this book....."Love is mean, but it's good."<br /> <br />This book is written from Caleb POV which a bonus in itself!!!!This book was soooooooooo good, a perfect ending to this f'ed up triangle....well square I guess!!!!!!!!!!  Read this book immediately but only if you've read the other books first...I love Caleb!! I'm sad that it's the end though....I can't wait to read more by this author!!!</span>

<div id="review_479822368" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/479822368" />
    <a title="Brenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna"><img alt="Brenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580475762p2/12928663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/479822368?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenna" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna">Brenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=drove-me-crazy">drove-me-crazy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer479822368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1108037307967783387"><i>
  <b>So many conflicting FEEEELINGS! *sigh*</b>
</i><br/><br/>Everyone knows by now what a crazy cluster fuck of awesome this series is. The characters are imperfect and flawed. They lie, cheat, steal, manipulate, and are extremely intense. It’s what I’ve loved about the Love Me With Lies series, it’s bold, it’s different, it’s smart. (Btw, you probably shouldn’t read this review if you haven’t read The Opportunist and Dirty Red)<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>The day I met her under that tree, it was as if I breathed a spore of her into my lu</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText1108037307967783387" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>So many conflicting FEEEELINGS! *sigh*</b>
</i><br /><br />Everyone knows by now what a crazy cluster fuck of awesome this series is. The characters are imperfect and flawed. They lie, cheat, steal, manipulate, and are extremely intense. It’s what I’ve loved about the Love Me With Lies series, it’s bold, it’s different, it’s smart. (Btw, you probably shouldn’t read this review if you haven’t read The Opportunist and Dirty Red)<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>The day I met her under that tree, it was as if I breathed a spore of her into my lungs. We kept coming back to each other. The distance between our bodies grew wider over the years as we tried to live separately. But that spore took root and grew. And no matter the distance or circumstance, Olivia is something that grows inside of me.</blockquote>
</i><br />When I started <i>Thief</i> I had this almost euphoric feeling. I was a giddy, grinning dork, eating up every word of Caleb’s love, devotion, and desire for Olivia. I wasn’t expecting there to be so much face time between Caleb and Olivia straight away and I was kind of excited about it, even though I wasn’t sure how it was going to go for the rest of the book. <br /><br />I equally loved the past and present shifts. Getting scenes from <i>The Opportunist</i> elaborated or from a different angle was really interesting and I didn’t find those scenes repetitive at all. They were extremely well done and entertaining. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>Chit-chattery. She just made up a word and used it in a sentence to insult me. God. Who the hell was this woman? And if I could get her to stop being hostile, what would she taste like?<br />…<br />This is how we’ve always hugged. She called it the Upper Cut. In college she would always say, ’ Upper cut me, Caleb.’ People would look at us like I was getting ready to hit her.</blockquote>
</i><br />Around the ½ way mark (maybe a little after), my feelings while reading this really changed. Something from the beginning kept eating at me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When we find out right in the beginning that Caleb hasn’t seen Estella is months and is not a part of her life, I was really sad. Then when it’s said that he didn’t get a paternity test and had NO PLANS TO I was completely dumbfounded. What!?!?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This decision by Caleb REALLLY got to me. The drama surrounding this specific issue was completely over the top, repetitive, and honestly just felt like drama for the sake of drama. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The going back and forth about Estella’s paternity was…. Ugh…. I can’t even explain how frustrated that made me. I didn’t find it clever or shocking. It didn’t feel like a twist to me. It was just annoying. I almost had to stop. I felt like lying about it once would have been fine, but multiple times? I just didn’t like it. And the whole issue could have been so easily avoided. I think that’s honestly what bothers me the most. Why did Caleb believe Leah?!?! EVER!?!? It makes zero sense. It makes him look gullible and stupid. I get that he’s a flawed character, that’s fine and it’s to be expected for him to screw up. But, this is something so <b>cut and dry. It’s science and law. She is either his daughter or not. There is no grey. </b>I just don’t know how he goes from the Caleb in <i>Dirty Red</i> - <i>“That was before you fucked with my daughter.”</i> to this guy who just walks away without a second thought that it might not be true!? Ok, sorry – rant over.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I love him.” <br />I cross the kitchen in two seconds. I grab her upper arm so she can’t get away and lean down until I’m right in her face. She has to see truth. My voice sounds more animal than human; a growl. <br />“More than me?” The light drains from her eyes and she tries to look away. <br />I shake her. “More than me?” <br />“I don’t love anything more than I love you.” My fingers tighten on her arm. <br />“Then why are we playing these stupid games?” </blockquote>
</i><br />I was asking the same question. Of course I expected there to be drama, lies, and it to be a rough road for these two, but at some point it was a bit too repetitive for me. Like I said, the first ½ or so was AMAZING, like 5+ star good but certain decisions and some of the drama got to me too much. I am glad I did end up finishing even though the ending felt a little rushed after the overload of events in the last 10-15%. About the ending…<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I of course am happy that Caleb and Olivia end up together. It’s sad that she didn’t get her baby, but at the same time their ending felt right to me. I feel like a baby would have been too cliché and predictable and after the clichéd paternity drama I’m glad it didn’t go that route. It wasn’t perfect, but at least they were together.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I am all for high emotions, turmoil, and books getting a huge reaction out of me. That is what I read for. But in this case, the issues affected the way I felt about the characters and made me lose interest. I actually started to not even care and that really sucked. I was so frustrated with myself at points that I couldn’t just go with it, I hate that I didn’t enjoy this like I wanted and expected to. <br /><br />The writing was phenomenal as always. I highlighted like CRAZY and could feel the intensity of everyone’s emotions through the pages. Even though this one wasn’t a favorite, I know it was for many and I still highly recommend this series! What a wild freaking ride!<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Eventually.” She sighs. “That word is so us, isn’t it? Eventually, you’ll tell me you’re faking your amnesia. Eventually, I’ll tell you that I’m pretending not to know you. Eventually, we’ll come back together, fall apart, come back together.”<br /></b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1108037307967783387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <u>Favorite Quotes/Lines:</u>
</b><br><br>"I want your babies, and your anger, and your cold blue eyes. I want to go on anniversary dinners with you, I want to wrap Christmas presents with you. I want to fight with you about stupid things and then hold you down in my bed and make it up to you. I want to have more cake batter fights and camping trips. I want your future, Olivia. Please come back to me."<br><br>"She has the kind of love that can stain your soul, make you beg not to have one, just to escape the spell she’s put you under. It keeps us alive."<br><br>"Wherever we go in the next life, we’ll be together," I say.<br>"Let’s not go to hell then, that’s where Leah will be."<br><br>"Maybe our souls touched underneath that tree. Maybe I decided to love her. Maybe love wasn't our choice. But when I looked at that woman, I saw myself differently."<br><br>"Olivia, I once told you that I would love again, and that you would hurt forever. Do you remember?" She nods. It’s a painful memory for both of us. "It was a lie. I knew it was a lie, even as I said it. I’ve never loved anyone after you. I never will." I walk out.<br>Walk away. No more fighting — not for her, or with her, or with myself.<br>I am so sad."<br><br>"She's mine. She always has been, she always will be. We've been running in opposite directions for the last ten years, and we collide at every turn. Sometimes, it's because we're looking for each other, other times it's fate."</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436134250?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather (hungrycookiemonster)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather (hungrycookiemonster)" href="/user/show/3152818-heather-hungrycookiemonster">Heather (hungrycookiemonster)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3152818-heather-hungrycookiemonster?shelf=adult">adult</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

I collect them so you don't have too. :p </b><br/><br/><br/><b> After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1784966.Dirty_Red' title='Dirty Red by Vickie M.   <span id="freeText1332294331409398877" style="display:none"><b> All teasers so far release included at the bottom. I collect them so you don't have too. :p </b><br /><br /><br /><b> After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1784966.Dirty_Red" title="Dirty Red by Vickie M. Stringer" rel="nofollow noopener">Dirty Red</a>:</b> <br /><br />I can't freaking wait for Caleb's novel after <i>Dirty Red </i>'s explosive ending. Plus, I'd really like to know what the present was. <br /><br /><br /><b> After the title release: </b><br /><br /><i>Thief? THIEF? </i> Caleb is going to be a thief? *dies with the hugest grin ever*<br /><br /><br /><b> After the cover release: </b><br /><br />HOT DAMN! Is that seriously Caleb? I want. Please. <br /><br />I heard a rumor <i> Thief </i> is expected to have a late 2013 release date. Please tell me it isn't so. I need <i> Thief </i> like tomorrow.<br /><br />***********************************************************************<br /><br /><b>Teaser 1:<br /><br /><i>Past </i></b> <br /><br />“Hey, handsome, what are you doing here?”<br /><br />I lifted my sunglasses and smiled.<br /><br />“Cammie?”<br /><br />She smirked and stood on her tiptoes to give me a hug. My eyes darted past her and searched the crowd walking into the mall.<br /><br />“Is she—?”<br /><br />She shook her head. “Not here.”<br /><br />I felt myself relax. I didn’t know if I could handle seeing her. Out of sight, partially out of mind was what was working for me at the moment.<br /><br />“So, what are you doing here? Shouldn’t you be home with the pregnant wifey witch?”<br /><br />We fell into step and I grinned at her. “I’m here for a pretzel actually. She had a craving.”<br /><br />“God, that’s embarrassing—once the big man on campus, now the bitch’s errand boy.”<br /><br />I laughed. Cammie was always good for a laugh. I held the door open for her, and the air conditioning blasted me in the face.<br /><br />“What are you doing here?”<br /><br />“Oh, you know me,” she sang stopping at a rack of skirts. “I like to spend money.”<br /><br />I nodded and stuck my hands in my pockets feeling awkward.<br /><br />“Actually,” she said turning to me. “I’m looking for a dress to wear to a fancy thing. Help me?”<br /><br />I shrugged. “Since when do you need help shopping?”<br /><br />“Oh, that’s right.” She tucked her lips in and shook her head. “You have to get back to your pregnant wife. Don’t let me hold you up.” She dismissed me with a wave of her hand and pulled a slinky white dress off the rack.<br /><br />I scratched the back of my head. “White washes you out.”<br /><br />She narrowed her eyes and put the dress back while still looking at me. “Who asked you?”<br /><br />She held up a blue silk dress for me to see and I nodded. She shoved it at me and I took it.<br /><br />“So, do you know what you’re having…boy…girl…seed of Chucky?”<br /><br />“We’re not finding out.”<br /><br />She tossed another dress my way. It was a hideous salmon color. I re-shelved it when she wasn’t looking.<br /><br />“I own a nanny agency you know. So, when the little bundle comes along, I’m sure I can find it a new mother.”<br /><br />She held up a Gucci dress and I nodded.<br /><br />“Since when do you like kids?” Cammie was about as maternal as a shark.<br /><br />“I don’t. I like money, and in Boca Raton, a nanny agency is good money.”<br /><br />I raised my eyebrows. “Leah will be be fine. You know I’m traditional about those things.”<br /><br />Cammie snorted. “You might be, but I highly doubt your lovely wife will be offering up the breast any time soon.”<br /><br />I ground my teeth together which she noticed right away.<br /><br />“Sore subject much? Don’t worry C—Dizzle, I’ve seen this before. Tell her you’ll buy her a new set when it’s all over. That should bring her around.”<br /><br />I cocked my head. That wasn’t a bad idea.<br /><br />I followed her to the changing room.<br /><br />“So,” I said, leaning against the wall outside. “How’s—“<br /><br />“She’s fine.”<br /><br />I nodded looking at the floor.<br /><br />“Is she—“<br /><br />She burst out wearing the blue dress and spun in a circle.<br /><br />“Don’t even bother trying the others on,” I said.<br /><br />She made a kissy face at the mirror and nodded. “You’re right.”<br /><br />The door slammed closed. A minute later she came out dressed and carrying the garment on her arm.<br /><br />“Well, that was easy.”<br /><br />I walked with her to the register and watched as she plucked out her credit card. “Now a gift and shoes and I’m all set.”<br /><br />“What’s the dress for?”<br /><br />She leveled her eyes on me, a wicked smile playing her lips.<br /><br />“Didn’t I tell you?” she said innocently. “This dress is for Olivia’s wedding.”<br /><br />A tremor of shock passed through me. Suddenly, all of the colors around me were bleeding together hurting my eyes. I felt sick, my chest constricting with each second that passed. Cammie’s lips were moving, she was saying something. I shook my head to clear it.<br /><br />“What?”<br /><br />She smirked at me and tossed her blonde hair over her shoulder. Then she patted my arm sympathetically.<br /><br />“Hurts, doesn’t it mother-fucker?”<br /><br />“When?” I breathed.<br /><br />“Uh, uh—I’m not telling you that.”<br /><br />I licked my lips. “Cammie…tell me it’s not Turner.”<br /><br />Her face broke into smile. “Nope.”<br /><br />I felt the pressure in my chest release a little. A little. I hated Turner. I hadn’t even met the guy. It was by sight alone.<br /><br />“Noah Stein.,” Cammie said, grinning. “Funny story,” she said making her eyes really big. “—She met him on that little impromptu trip she took to Rome. You remember? The one where she came bearing her soul, and you turned her away.”<br /><br />“It didn’t happen like that.”<br /><br />She cocked the corner of her mouth up and shook her head like she was disappointed in me. “You had your chance. Fate hates you guys.”<br /><br />“Leah had just lost the baby and her sister tried to commit suicide. I couldn’t leave her. I was trying to do the right thing for once.”<br /><br />She jerks to look at me. “Leah was…” her voice trails off and her eyes glaze over. I cock my head.<br /><br />“Leah lost a baby?” she repeated. I saw something in her eyes that made me take a step closer.<br /><br />“What are you not saying?”<br /><br />She pursed her lips and shook her head at me. “When you went to Rome with Leah, were you trying to have a baby?”<br /><br />Cammie was known for asking uncomfortable questions, but this was a little personal even for her.<br /><br />“No. We were just taking a break. Getting away from everything. Trying to work on-“<br /><br />“-Your marriage,” she finished.<br /><br />“Why are you asking me this?<br /><br />She suddenly looked up from the patch of floor she’d been staring at. “Just interested I guess. Hey, I’ve got to get out of here.”<br /><br />She leaned up to kiss me on the cheek, but something wasn’t sitting right with me. Cammie was an obnoxious spitfire. When she started acting awkward, something was wrong.<br /><br />“Cammie…”<br /><br />“Don’t,” she said. “She’s happy. She’s getting married. Leave her alone.”<br /><br />She started walking away, but I grabbed her wrist. “You said that to me once before, do you remember?”<br /><br />Her face paled. She yanked her arm away.<br /><br />“Just tell me when?” I pleaded. “Cammie, please…”<br /><br />She swallowed. “Saturday.”<br /><br />I closed my eyes, dropped my head. “Bye, Cam.”<br /><br />“Bye, Caleb.”<br /><br /><br /><b>Teaser 2<br /><br /><i>Past </i> </b><br /><br />The door was slightly ajar when I arrived. I was about to knock when it swung open and a man came out carrying a garbage bag. I stepped back too startled to speak. My thoughts spun in a hundred directions. He wasn’t her type. I was going to kill him. Why was he taking out her trash? Did he sleep here often? I waited for him to look up, thinking every man deserved a chance to explain himself before he got the shit beat out of him. <br /><br />He was mildly startled to see me standing in front of him. He looked past me to see if I was with someone else, and then said. <br /><br />“Help you?”<br /><br />He hadn’t pulled the door to Olivia’s apartment closed, and I could see inside. <br /><br />Empty. <br /><br />I felt the air leave my lungs. I closed my eyes tilting my head back. No, no, no. <br /><br />I walked away, my hands in my hair and circled back to where maintenance was looking at me curiously. My instant jealousy had caused me to miss the uniform and name badge. Why had I left her? Why hadn’t I just stayed? I knew she did this. She ran when she was afraid. I thought—<br /><br />What had I thought? That I could keep her because we’d made love? That her demons wouldn’t find her in the orange grove where I’d sold my soul to be with her? <br /><br />I eyed the badge clipped to the front of his shirt. <br /><br />“Miguel.” My voice sounded raw even to my ears. Miguel raised his eyebrows as he watched me struggle with a sentence. “When did she—? How long—?”<br /><br />“This one’s been open for twenty four hours,” he said, referring to the apartment behind him. “We have a waiting list. Have to make it ready for next tenants.”<br /><br />Twenty four hours? Where had she gone? Had she left right away? Had something scared her away? <br /><br />I ran a hand through my hair. I’d left her just two days ago to go settle my affairs. I’d danced with her in the parking lot before I’d left. She’d tried to tell me the truth, but I’d stopped her. When she found out about the amnesia, she’d think of every possible reason to run from me. I’d planned on locking her in the apartment; making love to her again and convincing her that we could make it work. But, first I’d had loose ends to tie up. <br /><br />I’d left Olivia and gone straight to Leah’s townhouse. When she opened the door I could tell she’d been crying. It took me thirty minutes to break her heart. It hurt me to do it. She had done nothing to deserve what I was doing to her. I told her I’d met someone. She didn’t ask who, though I suspected she knew since she’d followed me to Olivia’s apartment a few weeks earlier. Before I left, I kissed her forehead. I didn’t tell her about the amnesia. I didn’t want to hurt her any more than I already had. <br /><br />I went to my condo next. As I stood under the shower I thought of our week together. I thought of the orange grove; of the way she tasted, the way her skin felt like cold satin beneath my fingers. When my mind went to that first moment of being inside her; of the way her eyes had widened and her lips had parted, I had to blast myself with cold water. <br />She’d given me everything—everything she’d held back before. She was different. She was also the same; stubborn, defiant...full of lies. <br />I’d tried to break her before. Now, I just wanted her as she was. I wanted every, last beautiful flaw. I wanted the witty one liner’s, and the coldness that only I knew how to warm. I wanted the fight and the friction and the make- up sex. I wanted her to wake up in my bed every morning. I wanted her shitty cooking and her beautiful, complex mind. <br />I’d gone back on everything I believed, to be with her. I threw truth out the window. I was so afraid she’d forget about me, I’d lied to sneak back into her life. Now, I had inordinate amounts of explaining to do. <br /><br />I looked at Miguel. He suddenly seemed like my last remaining tie to her. <br /><br />“Did she leave anything?—a note….anything?”<br />Miguel rubbed the back of his neck. “No, man.”<br /><br />“Did she say where she was going?”<br /><br />He sucked his teeth. “I’m just maintenance. They don’t exactly give me a forwarding address.” He looked around to make sure we were alone. <br /><br />“But, if she did leave something it would be in this black garbage bag, which I’m going to set right here while I do a run through of the apartment.”<br /><br />He dropped the bag on the floor, and gave me a look before stepping back into the apartment and closing the door behind him. <br /><br />I picked it up, weighed it in my hand. It was light. Had she left me something, telling me where she’d gone? Had Jim come back and scared her off? Had he told her? I knelt down and turned the bag over, dumping its contents on the concrete. I was sweating and my hands were damp as I sifted through the trash. Ripped up papers, broken glass, crushed flower petals….what was I looking for? A letter? Olivia would never write me a letter. It wasn’t her style. This was her style; leaving me without notice…throwing me in the fire to burn. I tossed the bag. Half of my heart was breaking, the other half was hell fucking angry. As the bag fluttered to the ground, I heard the slight tinkering of something hitting the floor. My eyes scanned the concrete, desperate for anything that would lead me to her. <br /><br />I found it lying between my feet.<br /><br />A penny. <br /><br />Had she left it for me, or had she just left it? I picked it up, held it between my fingers. The once shiny surface had the slightly green tinge of aging copper. This was her goodbye? I felt anger and more than anger, I felt confusion. What had I done? The orange grove, the kiss in the parking lot before I’d left. I’d felt so sure of what I felt for her…what she felt for me. There was no way Olivia would have given herself to me if she wasn’t sure of us. Then why? <br />WHY?<br /><br />I walked to the edge of the parking lot and lifted my fist, the penny pressing against my palm. Toss it. I told myself. My muscles tensed to throw it. <br /><br />I couldn’t do it. My hand dropped to my side. I put the penny in my pocket and drove home. <br /><br /><br /><b>Teaser 3:<br /><br /><i>Past</i> </b><br /><br />I missed a shot. People were looking at me like I’d gunned down a gym full of people instead of shooting an air ball. My mother was always teasing me, telling me that I didn’t take anything seriously. Maybe, she was right up until now. I was taking Olivia Kaspen seriously. All five feet two inches of her. She was mouthy and condescending and she never smiled, but I liked her. I wanted to give her something. So I missed the shot.<br /><br />“Is it true?”<br /><br />I looked up from my plate of pancakes. Desiree, one of the cheerleaders slid into the seat opposite me. She was wearing her makeup from the night before and my buddy, Kiel’s jersey. Why did girl’s do that? Eerised.<br /><br />“Is what true?”<br /><br />“You missed the shot for a girl?”<br /><br />"Where did you hear that?” I pushed my plate away and took a sip of tea.<br /><br />“Everyone is talking about it.” She smirked at me and ripped off a piece of my pancake, sliding it between her teeth.<br /><br />I looked at her through narrowed eyes. I was having a hard time pulling off this charming act when my palms were sweating. “Who are they saying I did it for?” If people found out it was Olivia I’d missed the shot for, things would get very uncomfortable for her.<br /><br />Desiree sucked the syrup from her fingers. “Oh, there are rumors. Who knows if they’re true. You know how people can be.”<br /><br />I shrugged, trying to be nonchalant, but my shoulders were tensed.<br /><br />“Humor me, Des.”<br /><br />She pursed her lips and leaned forward. “A pre law major. No one really knows who she is. Some people say they saw you talking to her before you missed the shot.”<br /><br />“Maybe, my game was just off,” I said, setting my mug down and standing up.<br /><br />Desiree smiled up at me. “Maybe. If you ask me, it’s kind of romantic.”<br /><br />“Romantic?” I repeated.<br /><br />“Yeah. She must be something.”<br /><br />I leaned down until both of my hands were flat on the table and Desiree and I were on eye level.<br /><br />“Does that really sound like something I would do, Des?”<br /><br />She looked at me for a long minute before shaking her head.<br /><br />“Well, there you have your answer.”<br /><br />I left wiping my palms on my pant legs. How many people had seen me speaking to Olivia? It was a stupid…careless, but then I could have never anticipated her challenge. If things had gone my way, she would have agreed to a date for making the shot. Everyone would have walked away a winner aka. I would walked away the winner.<br /><br />I couldn’t help but smile as I jogged down the stairs in front of the dining hall. Forget it. Girls rarely surprised me. I would have missed that shot five hundred times for a date with her.<br /><br /><br /><b>Teaser 4 <br /><br /><i>Gardenia Bush</i> </b><br /><br />Once, during her senior year, she bought a gardenia bush to put outside her apartment. She fawned over that thing like it was a dog; googled ways to take care of it and then made notes in one of those spiral notebooks. She’d even named it-Patricia-I think. Every day she’d squat on her haunches outside her front door, and examine Patricia to see if it had bloomed a flower. I’d watch her face when she came back inside, she always wore this look of hopeful determination. Not yet-she’d say to me, as if all of her hope for life was tied in to that gardenia plant blooming a flower. That’s what I loved about her; that grim determination to survive even though the odds seemed to always be against her. Despite all of Olivia’s plant nurturing, Patricia had slowly started to fade away; her leaves curling at the tips and turning brown. Olivia would stare at that plant, a crease forming between her eyebrows and her little mouth puckered in a frown worth kissing. Florida had an especially cold winter the year. One morning when I got to her apartment Patricia was clearly dead. I’d jumped into my car and sped off to Home Depot where I’d seen them selling the same bushes. Before my little love cracked her eyes open, I’d replaced her dead plant with a healthy one, repotting it over the grass in front of her building. I’d thrown the old one in the dumpster and washed my hands in the pool before knocking on her door. She’d checked on it when she opened the door for me that morning, her eyes lighting up when she saw the healthy green leaves. I don’t know if she ever suspected what I’d done, she’d never said anything. I took care of it without her knowing. Sticking plant food into the pot before I knocked on her door. My mother always put used tea bags in the soil around her rose bushes. I did that a couple times too. Right before we broke up that damn plant bloomed a flower. I’d never seen her so excited. The look on her face was the same as when I’d missed the shot for her. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1332294331409398877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6332260601482030207"><b>Caleb Drake - Stealing Reader's Hearts One Chapter at a Time <3</b><br/><br/>*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*<br/><br/>I absolutely adore the Love Me With Lies series! I went into this book knowing that Caleb's point of view was going to be epic and all I can say is that Tarryn Fisher completely surpassed my already high expectations for the final book in Olivia and Caleb's story.<br/><br/>Since I don't want to give too much of this story away and spoil it for anyone, I will say that Thief continues where Dirty Red left off. </span>
  <span id="freeText6332260601482030207" style="display:none"><b>Caleb Drake - Stealing Reader's Hearts One Chapter at a Time &lt;3</b><br><br>*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*<br><br>I absolutely adore the Love Me With Lies series! I went into this book knowing that Caleb's point of view was going to be epic and all I can say is that Tarryn Fisher completely surpassed my already high expectations for the final book in Olivia and Caleb's story.<br><br>Since I don't want to give too much of this story away and spoil it for anyone, I will say that Thief continues where Dirty Red left off. Caleb made the decision to fight for a relationship with Olivia while dealing with the fall-out of his divorce from Leah. Is he too late to win her back? Will love be enough to make a relationship between the two of them work? Can they overcome all the lies, manipulation, and pain they caused each other in the past? Read Thief to find out!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418307i/828189.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>What you can expect from Thief:</b><br>*It will wreck you emotionally<br>*It will give you multiple heart orgasms (yes this is my new favorite phrase he he)<br>*You will probably end up loving Caleb even more than you could have ever possibly imagined<br>*Most of your questions from The Opportunist &amp; Dirty Red will finally be answered<br>*You will finally find closure in regards to the Caleb and Olivia's relationship<br><br><b>Thank you Tarryn, from the bottom of my heart, for sharing Olivia and Caleb's beautiful story with your PLN's! &lt;3</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418307i/828190.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_483378234" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/483378234" />
    <a title="Audrie Cruz-Sealey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6725501-audrie-cruz-sealey"><img alt="Audrie Cruz-Sealey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319074319p2/6725501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/483378234?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Audrie Cruz-Sealey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Audrie Cruz-Sealey" href="/user/show/6725501-audrie-cruz-sealey">Audrie Cruz-Sealey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer483378234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer908173560545587381">Dear Tarryn,<br/><br/>Now I know that you like to evoke emotion in your books...and you have, you have :)<br/><br/>I know that a lot of your readers have felt giddy, frustrated, have wanted to reach into books and slap people, have felt disappointed, angry, hopeful....<br/><br/>If it is not to much to ask...we need the HEA, we crave the HEA, please do not shatter me...please bring them together (preferably without hurting the Hot Ghandi to badly and feel free to CrUsH Leah).<br/><br/>Thanks,<br/><br/>Audrie</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_519566626" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/519566626" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/519566626?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer519566626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18440865166174921665"><b>7/22/13<br/>Oh my HEART!! I can't believe it's OVER!! I'm emotionally battered from the highs and lows, but OMG, I loved it!! Brilliant!</b><br/><br/><br/><b>**Thoughts immediately after reading Dirty Red back in January**</b><br/><br/>If Caleb and Olivia do not end up together I will HAVE TO HURT SOMEONE!!!<br/><br/>I'm dying for this book, literally! <br/><br/><b>8/1/13 And now for the "real" review:</b><br/><br/>Thief was a perfectly imperfect ending to a series I will never forget. I felt like my heart and head went through the spin cycle from all the highs and lows I</span>
  <span id="freeText18440865166174921665" style="display:none"><b>7/22/13<br />Oh my HEART!! I can't believe it's OVER!! I'm emotionally battered from the highs and lows, but OMG, I loved it!! Brilliant!</b><br /><br /><br /><b>**Thoughts immediately after reading Dirty Red back in January**</b><br /><br />If Caleb and Olivia do not end up together I will HAVE TO HURT SOMEONE!!!<br /><br />I'm dying for this book, literally! <br /><br /><b>8/1/13 And now for the "real" review:</b><br /><br />Thief was a perfectly imperfect ending to a series I will never forget. I felt like my heart and head went through the spin cycle from all the highs and lows I experienced, but I loved every minute of it! I think one of things that stand out about this series is the realistic way it showed the deep hurt felt from heartache, regret, and loving “the one,” and then screwing it up. It’s easy to see and relate our imperfect selves in each of these characters, well maybe except for Leah, I hope….<br /><br />After all the years and going back and forth with Olivia, Caleb commits to Olivia being the only girl for him and he intends to be with her for good. One huge problem is that she moved on and married someone else, Noah. After all the years, and the fact that Caleb chose to stay with Leah after Olivia bared her heart to him, she gave up, and resigned herself to the fact Caleb and her would never be together. Noah came along and even though Olivia knew she could never love anyone as much or like Caleb, she had to let go. So she let down her defenses and allowed some of her heart to love Noah. Caleb has his work cut out for him, but he is DETERMINED:<br /><b>
  <i><br />“This is the last time I’m going to say this, so listen carefully,” I can smell her skin. “You and I are happening. No one is keeping us apart again. Not Noah or Cammie, and least of all, f**king Leah. You are mine. Do you understand me?”</i>
</b><br /><br />I’m not a fan of cheating stories, but to be honest I was rooting for Caleb the whole time. I felt a little justified in this because Noah married Olivia knowing she would never truly love him with her whole heart. I think on some level Noah knew that they wouldn’t and couldn’t last. I could just care less about Leah, she had no heart in my opinion, and I was so happy Caleb finally saw through all her schemes at the end of Dirty Red. Leah (gag!) finally gets a little of what was coming to her and I couldn’t have smiled bigger in that scene! <br /><br />I loved getting Caleb’s POV. Being in his head showed me that he was just as obsessed with Olivia as she was with him. It also showed me that they were a perfect match. He loved her faults and all. In fact her faults may have made him love her more. It cracked me up when he would call her things like “my little prude” or “the little witch” showing how he really adored the weaknesses in her. Love this quote:<br /><b>
  <i><br />“You’re crazy and erratic and mean, but I’ll never complain about your taste in music.” <br />“I’m sorry,” she says, setting down the iPod and staring at me. “Aren’t you supposed to be charming me this weekend?”<br />I grab her knee and squeeze. “That’s what I’m doing, Duchess. A compliment with an insult. Just the way you like it.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Both Olivia and Caleb left a path of destruction and hurt, and have the scars to show it. But after all is said and done these two still are in love with each other, obsessed with each other, and really are complete soul mates! I think they needed all this time to grow and learn to really appreciate their once in a lifetime love and connection. <br /><br />I’m so sad to say good bye to this series. This is a series I won’t, and can’t forget. The emotional lows gutted me and the highs left me soaring! I have so many passages highlighted (11 pages on my kindle) and every time I go back to look at a quote I end up highlighting more!! I’ve pimped this story out to whoever will listen and if you haven’t yet picked up this series, you are missing out!! Thank you Tarryn! </span>
  <a data-text-id="18440865166174921665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_483706428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/483706428" />
    <a title="Luisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2893615-luisa"><img alt="Luisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343069084p2/2893615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/483706428?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luisa" href="/user/show/2893615-luisa">Luisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2893615-luisa?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2893615-luisa?shelf=british-book-boyfriends">british-book-boyfriends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer483706428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10856449380446627738">As a fan of the Love Me With Lies series, I had been anticipating the release of Thief with much excitement. I had high expectations for this book and it didn't disappoint. If you are familiar with Tarryn Fisher's writing, you know she has raised the bar for all indie contemporary writers. <br/>Thief ties up all the loose ends for this series, and Caleb's point of view is enlightening and intense. Definitely a hard book to put down; you will devour this book in one sitting.<br/><br/>Plot:<br/><br/>After a messy divorce,</span>
  <span id="freeText10856449380446627738" style="display:none">As a fan of the Love Me With Lies series, I had been anticipating the release of Thief with much excitement. I had high expectations for this book and it didn't disappoint. If you are familiar with Tarryn Fisher's writing, you know she has raised the bar for all indie contemporary writers. <br />Thief ties up all the loose ends for this series, and Caleb's point of view is enlightening and intense. Definitely a hard book to put down; you will devour this book in one sitting.<br /><br />Plot:<br /><br />After a messy divorce, Caleb Drake is determined to fight for the love of his life -Olivia Kaspen. The bad news is that she's not longer waiting around for him, she has moved on and is happily married. Or at least that's what it seems. Once again, destiny brings these two star-crossed lovers to be honest with their feelings when Caleb finds himself in a complicated situation, in which he has to protect Olivia from a obsessive criminal on the loose. <br />After 10+ years, Caleb is done playing games. Thief is cutthroat and honest, but will Caleb and Olivia's relationship be still overshadow by the sins of their past? Will these two have a chance to redeem for their mistakes? Will they finally have a chance to utter all the words that went unsaid?<br />Buckle up and get ready to be shocked, overwhelmed, and overjoyed, all in the same ride. As per usual, you will be riding a roller coaster of emotions, this time into their final destination.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10856449380446627738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer685539720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16814743652964309316">“Forget all you know — I said to myself. This is the one you belong with. I don’t know how I knew that. Maybe our souls touched underneath that tree. Maybe I decided to love her. Maybe love wasn’t our choice. But when I looked at that woman, I saw myself differently. And it wasn’t in a good light. Not a thing would keep me from her. And that could make a person do things they never thought themselves capable of. What I felt for her scared the hell out of me. It was a consuming obsession.”<br/>- Caleb</span>
  <span id="freeText16814743652964309316" style="display:none">“Forget all you know — I said to myself. This is the one you belong with. I don’t know how I knew that. Maybe our souls touched underneath that tree. Maybe I decided to love her. Maybe love wasn’t our choice. But when I looked at that woman, I saw myself differently. And it wasn’t in a good light. Not a thing would keep me from her. And that could make a person do things they never thought themselves capable of. What I felt for her scared the hell out of me. It was a consuming obsession.”<br />- Caleb Drake<br /><br />* * *<br />“My heart is still broken. I’m trying to figure out how to live without what I really want. That includes letting go of old dreams and making some new ones. I think, anyway.”<br />- Caleb Drake<br /><br />* * *<br />“She is the only one who makes me want to be a better person … and a better person for her. I don’t even need to be good, I just need to be good for her.”<br />- Caleb Drake<br /><br />* * *<br />“Most men like danger. There is nothing sweeter than a dangerous woman. Makes us feel a little manlier to be able to call them ours.”<br />- Steve<br /><br />* * *<br />“I lost interest in healthy women shortly after meeting Olivia. It’s a curse. After tasting her, I’ve rarely found a woman who I actually think is interesting. I like her darkness, her ever present sarcasm, the way she makes me work for every smile — every kiss. I like how strong she is, how hard she fights for things. I love how weak I make her. I might be her only weakness. I earned that spot and I very much want to keep it.”<br />- Caleb Drake<br /><br />* * *<br />“Life does not accommodate you, it shatters you. Love is mean, but it’s good. It keeps us alive. I”<br />- Luca<br /><br />* * *<br />“You couldn’t get rid of the past. You couldn’t ignore it, or bury it, or throw it over the balcony. You just had to learn to live beside it. It had to peacefully co-exist with your present. If I could figure out how to do that, I could be okay.”<br />- Olivia Kaspen<br /><br />* * *<br />“Love is a God-given tool, she tells me. It screws things back in place that were loose, and it cleans out all the broken pieces that you don’t need anymore.”<br />- Olivia Kaspen</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LzCHjAGR+nD51qmuZ5I2VcB0nQqupDSKf+nirQhw+0QVFu5eus8zGF79Hc+QZzyKFit6wmApuu0kl6QcxTMJ3g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8RiQVlCunf291eMlTQt/4ZTI3A8R8JM9+5ZzwiqNkiHLPvmE6/BUlRr+V0S6/nU+Qpc7x999HVqg6DVz585guw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14795252499059910898">I would like to write a novel that every, single person loves, but not even J.K. Rowling could do that. Instead, I try to write stories that pull on people's emotions. I believe that sadness is the most powerful emotion, and swirled with regret the two become a dominating force. I love villains. Three of my favorites are Mother Gothel, Gaston and the Evil Queen who all suffered from a pretty wicke</span>
  <span id="freeText14795252499059910898" style="display:none">I would like to write a novel that every, single person loves, but not even J.K. Rowling could do that. Instead, I try to write stories that pull on people's emotions. I believe that sadness is the most powerful emotion, and swirled with regret the two become a dominating force. I love villains. Three of my favorites are Mother Gothel, Gaston and the Evil Queen who all suffered from a pretty wicked case of vanity (like me). I like to make these personality types the center of my stories. <br />I love rain, Coke, Starbucks and sarcasm. I hate bad adjectives and the word "smolder". If you read my book-I love you. If you hate my book-I still love you, but please don't be mean to me; I'm half badass, half cry baby. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14795252499059910898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
